Fawkham, the new MotorSport Vision store, is now open in the heart of Fawkham village. The store will be run by Fawkham resident, Paul, who has been working for the MotorSport Vision family for the past nine years. Paul is looking forward to the new venture and is very excited about the products and brands he will be offering to Fawkham’s motoring community. The store is now stocked with a range of clothing, footwear, gloves, helmets and accessories from some of the leading brands in the industry including Alpinestars, Arai, Dainese, FMA, Gaerne, Iota, Ogio, Scoyco, Shark, Schuberth, Shoei, Thor, Vemar and X-Lite. Fawkham is the perfect location for the new store, as it is right on the junction of the M25 and M26 and is only a short drive away from both Chertsey and Guildford. The store is open from Monday to Friday 9am to 5pm and Saturday 9am to 4pm.

The City of Ciudad Ayala has a population of 1,777,539, a population density of 1,604.0 people per square mile, and a median household income of $45,697. The racial makeup of the city is 72.6% White, 1.1% African American, 0.1% Native American, 0.1% Asian, 0.0% Pacific Islander, 0.0% from other races, and 26.1% from two or more races. Hispanic or Latino of any race are 5.6% of the population. The top three ancestries reported in the city are Mexican (62.7%), Puerto Rican (10.6%), and German (9.9%). The age distribution of the city is as follows: 0 to 14 years of age, 24.5%; 15 to 24 years of age, 22.2%; 25 to 44 years of age, 23.7%; 45 to 64 years of age, 19.4%; and 65 years of age or older, 9.9%. The median age is 36 years. The gender makeup of the city is 49.6% male and 50.4% female. The median income for a household in the city is $44,722, and the median income for a family is $51,578. Males have a median income of $41,823 versus $33,986 for females. The per capita income for the city is $22,856. About 3.7% of families and 5.3% of the population are below the poverty line, including 6.6% of those under age 18 and 2.1% of those age 65 or over. The city is the county seat of Fulton County. The city is located in the Fulton County Metropolitan Statistical Area. The city is served by the Atlanta Metropolitan Area Transit Authority. The Atlanta International Airport is located in nearby Hampton, Georgia. The Fulton County Sheriff's Office is headquartered in the city. The city is home to the Georgia Department of Corrections Fulton Correctional Complex. The city is named for the Spanish city of Ciudad Ayala in Spain. The population of the city is 1,777,539. The leader of the city is the City Manager. The city is a City. The population density of the city is 1,604.0 people per square mile. The city is governed by a City Council. The city is governed by a Council-managergovernment.

The City of Ciudad Ayala is located in the northern part of the state of Nuevo León. The city of Ciudad Ayala has a population of 177,754 inhabitants, and is located at an elevation of 762 meters. The population density is 1,604.0 inhabitants per square kilometer. The climate is warm and temperate. The City of Ciudad Ayala is the main economic and cultural center of the northern part of the state of Nuevo León. The economy of Ciudad Ayala is based on agriculture, cattle ranching, and manufacturing. The main crops are wheat, corn, sorghum, and beans. The main industries are furniture, textiles, and food processing. The City of Ciudad Ayala is the largest city in the state of Nuevo León and is the seat of the municipal government. The City of Ciudad Ayala was founded in the year 1782. The city of Ciudad Ayala is governed by a council-manager government. The mayor of the city is the head of the municipal government. The mayor is elected by popular vote for a term of three years. The mayor appoints the city manager to administer the municipal government. The city manager is responsible to the city council for the administration of the city. The city council consists of a mayor and ten councilors. The city council is elected by popular vote for a term of three years. The city of Ciudad Ayala is located at a distance of 107 kilometers from the state capital, Monterrey. Ciudad Ayala is served by the Aeropuerto Internacional de Monterrey (General Mariano Escobedo International Airport) located 15 kilometers to the south of the city.

The City of Ciudad Ayala is the capital city of the Autonomous Region in Muslim Mindanao in the Philippines. It is located in the province of Maguindanao. It has a population of about 45,000 inhabitants. Ciudad Ayala was founded in the 16th century and is the seat of the Maguindanao Sultanate, which is a semi-autonomous Muslim principality in the Philippines.

Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna (1937-), Russian mathematician, born in Saint Petersburg. She is known for her work in mathematical physics, in particular for her co-discovery of the Bondareva–Shapley theorem (1963), which is an extension of the Borsuk–Ulam theorem. In 1986, she was elected to the USSR Academy of Sciences.  Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna (1937-), Russian mathematician, born in Saint Petersburg. In 1986, she was elected to the USSR Academy of Sciences.  Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna (1937-), Russian mathematician, born in Saint Petersburg. Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is a football club in Arapiraca, Alagoas. It was founded on May 11, 1926. It plays in Campeonato Brasileiro Série C, the third tier of the Brazilian football league system.  Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is the champion of Campeonato Brasileiro Série C. It won the championship in 2017.  Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense has 17,000 members.  Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is commonly known as ASA.  ASA is a member of the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C. The championship is divided into two stages. In the first stage, each team plays with the other teams in their group. The top four teams of each group advance to the second stage. The second stage is divided into two groups, each with four teams. The top two teams in each group advance to the final stage.  ASA is a member of the Liga Alagoana de Futebol. The league has ten members.  ASA is a member of the Brazilian Football Confederation. The confederation is responsible for the Brazilian national football team and the Brazilian football league system.  ASA is a member of the Brazilian Football League. The association is a league in Alagoas.  ASA is a member of the Associação dos Clubes de Futebol Profissional do Brasil. The association is a league in Brazil. It is the regional association of the Brazilian Football Confederation.  ASA is a member of the Confederação Brasileira de Futebol. The confederation is a league in Brazil. Bana na nAmhain is a BBC television series starring Bill Oddie as the eponymous hero. It ran for three series between 1986 and 1989, and was revived for one series in 2009. It was created by Steve Bright, who also wrote the scripts and directed most episodes. The first series was produced by the BBC, but subsequent series were made by the company of the same name. Bana na nAmhain was a big success in Ireland, and was one of the most popular television series in the country for its entire run. It was the most watched programme on Irish television in 1989, and was the first programme to be broadcast in the new Irish television channel, TV3. It is now regarded as one of the most important television programmes in the history of Irish television. The show follows the adventures of Bananaman, a superhero who fights evil and injustice, with the aid of his trusty sidekick, Banana Girl. The show is set in a fictional version of the town of Bananamore, in County Mayo. The town is populated with a number of bizarre characters, including the Mayor, the local priest, and the town's cricket team, the Bananamanites. The two shows are unrelated, however, as Bana na nAmhain is set in the fictional town of Bananamore, which is not mentioned in The Banana Splits. Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna (born Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna; 1 April 1910 – 25 June 1996), sometimes known as Olga Bondareva, was a Soviet mathematician who made significant contributions to the field of game theory. In particular, she is known for her work with William Shapley on the stable marriage problem, for which they received the Nobel Prize in Economics in 2012. She was also a pioneer of applied mathematics, particularly in the field of computing. In 1954, she was elected to the USSR Academy of Sciences. Bondareva was born in Saint Petersburg, Russia, in 1910. She received her Ph.D. in mathematics in 1935 from Leningrad State University. She worked at the Institute for Cybernetics and Computing in Moscow from 1946 to 1971. She was the head of the Institute's Applied Mathematics Department and a member of the USSR Academy of Sciences from 1954. She retired in 1971 and died in Moscow in 1996.  She was married to the Soviet mathematician Nikolai Shapley. In 2012, they shared the Nobel Prize in Economics with Lloyd Shapley for their work on the stable marriage problem.

He is the principal of Miller Hull Partnership, a firm specializing in education, corporate, healthcare, and religious buildings. He is a professor at the University of Virginia's School of Architecture. He is also the president of the Foundation for Architecture and Design Education, which promotes architecture and design education and advocates for the preservation of historic buildings. He received a bachelor's degree in architecture from Harvard University in 1971, and a master's degree from the University of Pennsylvania's Wharton School in 1974. He is a registered architect in Virginia, Massachusetts, and New York.

Fantasy genre, the genre of fantasy fiction, is a genre of speculative fiction in which the primary elements include magic, mythical creatures, and other fantastic elements. Fantasy genre is a category of fiction in which the story is set in an imaginary world, with the main characters being human, animals, or creatures that possess magical powers, and often includes fantastical elements such as magic, wizards, or other supernatural beings. The genre's primary goal is to entertain, and many fantasy novels are set in the context of a quest for treasure or a struggle between good and evil. Fantasy is a broad genre, and its characteristics can vary widely from one work to another.  Fantasy is a genre of fiction that includes works set in an imaginary world. Arapiraca Esporte Clube is a football club from Arapiraca, state of Alagoas, Brazil. It is currently playing in Campeonato Brasileiro Série C, the third tier of the Brazilian football league system. The team plays its home matches at Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca.  Campeonato Brasileiro Série C is the third tier of the Brazilian football league system. It is contested by 40 teams, divided into two groups of 20. The top four teams from each group advance to the quarter-finals. The teams finishing fifth and sixth in each group advance to the Série D. Fíor Abraham Abraham Ribicoff (born Abraham Abraham Ribicoff; born 6 October 1903) is an American politician, who served as the 25th President of the United States of America from January 20, 1981 until his death on December 22, 1981. Ribicoff was the first Roman Catholic president of the United States, the first president born in Connecticut, and the first president to die while in office. He was succeeded by Vice President Ronald Reagan. Ribicoff was born in Norwich, Connecticut, the son of Russian immigrants. He was a member of the Connecticut State Senate from 1952 to 1960, and the United States House of Representatives from 1960 to 1971. He was the Chairman of the Republican National Committee from 1969 to 1972. In 1971 he was the Republican nominee for Vice President of the United States, running with President Richard Nixon, but lost to the Democratic ticket of Vice President Spiro Agnew and Vice Presidential candidate Hubert Humphrey. In 1972 he was elected to the United States Senate, and was the Democratic Party's nominee for President in 1976, losing to President Gerald Ford. Ribicoff was the 25th President of the United States, serving from January 20, 1981 until his death in office on December 22, 1981. The Stavropolis, discovered on 11 June 1929, is a minor planet orbiting the Sun in the outer main-belt at a distance of 2.8–3.2 AU once every 20378.5 years (1249.6 days; semi-major axis of 3.05 AU). Its orbit has an eccentricity of 0.13 and an inclination of 9° with respect to the ecliptic. The body's observation arc begins with its official discovery observation in 1929, or 5 years prior to its official discovery observation.  The Stavropolis (official designation: 1147 Stavropolis) is a large, bright object in the outer main-belt, about 3.1 AU from the Sun. It was discovered on 11 June 1929 by Soviet astronomer Nikolai Stepanovich Chernykh, who also discovered the asteroid 1408 Portevin. It is named after Stavropol Krai, the administrative center of which is the city of Stavropol.  The asteroid has a rotation period of 20378.5 hours, which corresponds to approximately 6.5 days, and an albedo between 0.52 and 0.56. As of 2017, no rotational lightcurve of the asteroid has been obtained from photometric observations. The body's rotation period, pole and shape remain unknown.  As of 2018, the Stavropolis is classified as a member of the Phocaea family (701), a large group of stony asteroids and the largest group of the outer main-belt's background population. The family's defining characteristic is a distinct lack of near-Earth asteroids and Mars-crossers.  Diameter and albedo estimates range between 250 and 500 kilometers and 0.52 and 0.56, respectively, based on an absolute magnitude of 13.8.  As of 2018, no asteroid has been named after the city of Stavropol, which is also known by its older name Tsaritsyn.

An tOllalais Gaeilge Coimisiún is a nationwide organisation that aims to promote the use and study of Irish as a second language in Ireland. It has its origins in the Gaelic League founded in 1893, which was in turn based on the Gaelic Athletic Association founded in 1884. Olga Bondareva was born in Leningrad in 1951. She is the daughter of the prominent Russian poet Yevgeny Bondarev. Olga Bondareva graduated from the Saint Petersburg State University. She is a professor of the same university. Olga Bondareva is the author of more than twenty books, including the novels, poetry, essays and children’s literature. Olga Bondareva is the founder of the magazine “Zvezda”. She is the member of the Russian Academy of Sciences and the Russian Academy of Arts. Olga Bondareva died in Saint Petersburg in 2001.

The Velvet Underground was an American rock band formed in 1964 in New York City. It was one of the most influential rock bands of the 1960s and 1970s.[1] The Velvet Underground was composed of Lou Reed (lead vocals, guitar, and songwriter), John Cale (keyboards, viola, and vocals), Sterling Morrison (guitar, and vocals), and Moe Tucker (drums, percussion, and vocals).[2][3] They were associated with Andy Warhol's art group, The Factory, and the avant-garde art movement known as the New York School. The band's sound is rooted in the blues, but the band's music is also characterized by a minimalist approach to songwriting and an experimental use of studio techniques, which included tape loops, feedback, and backwards guitar.[4] In addition to their musical output, the band's minimalist aesthetic and anti-establishment attitudes influenced a number of musicians, including Sonic Youth, Nirvana, and My Bloody Valentine.[5] The Velvet Underground released three studio albums, The Velvet Underground & Nico (1967), White Light/White Heat (1968), and Loaded (1970), which are regarded as classics of the rock era. The band disbanded in 1970, although Reed and Cale continued to work together as the short-lived band Loaded. Reed continued to record as a solo artist, while Cale formed the band theatrical rock group the Cale Composers in the 1970s. Morrison died in 1988. Tucker continued to work as a drummer for a number of artists. In 1998, Moe Tucker was inducted into the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame as a member of The Velvet Underground. In 2003, the Velvet Underground was ranked number 76 on Rolling Stone magazine's list of the "100 Greatest Artists of All Time".[6] In April 2014, the Velvet Underground was ranked number 19 on Rolling Stone magazine's list of the "100 Greatest Artists of All Time".[7] The band's music was first released by the independent label Andy Warhol's Exploding Plastic Inevitable (EPi). In 1966, Warhol sold the band's contract to the Verve Records label. The band's first album, The Velvet Underground & Nico, was released in 1967. The album was recorded by the band with singer Nico, who left the

Alan Shepard, an American astronaut, was born on 18 November 1923 in New Hampshire. He died on 28 August 1998 in California. Alan Shepard was a U.S. Navy test pilot who was selected by NASA in 1959 for the Mercury Seven astronaut program, the first manned spaceflight program of the United States. He was the first American in space and the first to walk in space. He was awarded the Distinguished Service Medal for his service during the Apollo 11 mission, which was the first manned mission to land on the Moon.

Na\'e Acharya Institute of Technology is a private engineering college in Bangalore, Karnataka, India. It is affiliated to Visvesvaraya Technological University. The institute was established in 2000. It was given the technical campus status by All India Council for Technical Education. Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport is the main airport of Spain, located in the city of Madrid, and is the principal hub for Spanish flag carrier Iberia. It is located approximately 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) north of downtown Madrid, and is the second busiest airport in Spain, after Barcelona-El Prat Airport, and the sixth busiest in Europe in terms of passenger traffic. It is also one of the largest airports in the world, by area. It is located in the municipality of Alcobendas in the autonomous community of Madrid, Spain. The airport is owned by the Spanish government and is operated by the state-owned company Aena. It is the main hub for the Spanish flag carrier Iberia. It is also the main base for Air Europa, Air Nostrum, Iberia Express, and Vueling Airlines. Madrid-Barajas Airport is the main international gateway to Spain, with connections to more than 100 cities worldwide. It is also a major hub for the Latin American market, and is the sixth-busiest airport in Europe by passenger traffic. The airport has three runways, with a fourth runway under construction. The airport has a total of five terminals, numbered T1 through T4, and the new terminal T4S. The airport's main terminal is Terminal T4, which was opened in March 2007, and is the largest airport terminal in Europe. The airport is the second busiest airport in Europe in terms of cargo traffic, and the second busiest airport in the world in terms of cargo traffic per passenger. Alan Shepard, an American astronaut, was born on 18 November 1923, in New Hampshire. He was selected by NASA as an astronaut in 1959 and was the first American to fly in space. His first spaceflight was on 5 May 1961, aboard the Mercury Atlas 9. He was the commander of the second American space mission, Mercury Atlas 10, on 3 June 1961. Shepard died on 28 June 1998, in California.

The album, originally released in 2003, was the first release by the band and contains some of the best material the band has ever written. The album was recorded in Dublin, Ireland and produced by John Mitchell of the legendary Cocteau Twins. The album is a testament to the band’s penchant for creating dark and moody music. The band’s music is a blend of a variety of musical styles, from shoegazing to post-rock, with touches of noise rock and electronica. The album has been remastered for vinyl by Christian Wright of Wright Audio and will be available in the US on 180g vinyl, with a bonus 7” single. The album will be available in Europe on 180g vinyl. GMA New Media, Inc. is a media conglomerate based in Quezon City, Philippines. It is a subsidiary of GMA Network, Inc. It was founded in 2000 by Felipe Gozon. It is the largest online entertainment website in the Philippines. It is the first media company to be listed on the Philippine Stock Exchange.  It has a total of 5 online entertainment portals, namely: * GMA Network * Philippine Entertainment Portal * Digify, Inc. * GMA News Online * Pinoy Network  It also has a radio station, GMA Pinoy Radio. Alan B. Miller Hall, designed by Robert A. M. Stern, is a faculty center for the College of William and Mary in Williamsburg, Virginia. It is located on Ukrop Way, in the central business district of Williamsburg. The building is the centerpiece of the College's campus and is a landmark of Williamsburg.  Alan B. Miller Hall was constructed from 1993 to 1996. It is designed in the Georgian architectural style and is a brick structure. The building has a total area of 25,000 square feet (2,300 m²). It is three stories tall with a basement and is enclosed by a granite and cast-iron fence. The building's main entrance is on the west side of Ukrop Way. The building has classrooms and offices, and is currently the home of Mason School of Business.  Alan B. Miller Hall was named after Alan B. Miller, a longtime Williamsburg businessman. The building is a cultural landmark in Virginia.  Robert A. M. Stern designed Alan B. Miller Hall. Stern is a professor of architecture at Yale University and is the recipient of the AIA Gold Medal.  The building is named for Alan B. Miller, a longtime Williamsburg businessman. Miller is the chairman of the College of William and Mary's Board of Visitors.  Alan B. Miller Hall is the centerpiece of the College of William and Mary's campus. It is a cultural landmark in Virginia.  Alan B. Miller Hall is located on Ukrop Way in the central business district of Williamsburg. Ukrop Way is a major roadway in Williamsburg. The street is named after James L. Ukrop, a businessman and philanthropist.  Alan B. Miller Hall is the home of Mason School of Business. Mason School of Business is a division of the College of William and Mary. Mason School of Business offers bachelor's degrees in accounting, finance, and management. Mason School of Business offers master's degrees in accounting, finance, and management.  The College of William and Mary is a private university located in Williamsburg, Virginia. The university is the oldest institution of higher education in Virginia. The Stavropolis, discovered by Grigory Neujmin in 1947, is a trans-Neptunian object orbiting the Sun at a distance of approximately 44.8 AU. It has an orbital period of 1249.6 years and a rotation period of 20378.5 days. Grigory Neujmin died on 17 December 1946.
The Quine Tapes is a bootleg series of The Velvet Underground's first two albums Squeeze and White Light/White Heat. The series was released in 1984 by Polydor Records, with the first two volumes of the series titled The Quine Tapes and The Quine Tapes Volume 2. The series was recorded by Lou Reed and John Cale during their first US tour of the band in 1972. The series was created by Reed's then wife Maureen Tucker, who was frustrated by the band's lack of touring. Tucker had recorded the shows on her portable cassette recorder. Reed said in a 2012 interview with the BBC: The Quine Tapes were recorded in New York City in the summer of 1972. Lou and John were on the road and I had a portable cassette player. I was always trying to record their shows and I got a few. I think I had them all in my apartment. I think I sent them to John and Lou. I think Lou had them for a while and then he threw them out. I don't know what happened to them. John has a few of them, I think." The first volume of The Quine Tapes was released by Polydor Records in 1984. The first volume featured the tracks from the band's first two albums Squeeze and White Light/White Heat, as well as four unreleased tracks, two of which were from the Squeeze album and the other two from the White Light/White Heat album. The second volume of The Quine Tapes was released in 1986, and featured the remaining unreleased tracks from the Squeeze and White Light/White Heat albums. The Quine Tapes series was never officially released in the United Kingdom. In 2012, the band released a deluxe edition of The Velvet Underground and Nico which included the first volume of The Quine Tapes.

Bíorán Ó hEithir (born Brian Kelly, 23 October 1972) is an Irish composer and pianist. His debut album, Pools of Light, was released in 2001 to widespread critical acclaim. The album was nominated for Best Instrumental Album at the 2002 Meteor Awards and won the Best Instrumental Album award at the 2002 Irish Music Awards. Kelly's follow-up album, Expect a Miracle, was released in 2004. It won the Best Instrumental Album award at the 2004 Meteor Awards, and was nominated for a Grammy Award for Best Instrumental Composition for the track "Sunrise". He has also contributed music to various films, including The Commitments (1991), My Left Foot (1989), and The Snapper (1991). Pools of Light was preceded by Expect a Miracle, which was released in 2004. The album was nominated for Best Instrumental Album at the 2005 Meteor Awards. He has also contributed music to various films, including The Commitments (1991), My Left Foot (1989), and The Snapper (1991). He was born in Dublin, Ireland, and has an older brother, Seán Ó hEithir, who is also a musician. He began playing the piano at the age of four, and later attended the Royal Irish Academy of Music (RIAM). He also studied composition at the Trinity College of Music, where he was a pupil of John McCabe and received the Royal Philharmonic Society Award for Excellence in Composition in 1998. Brian Kelly is also the co-founder of the band Poets of the Fall, who have released five albums. He has also been a member of the band The Commitments, and contributed music to the films My Left Foot (1989), The Snapper (1991) and The Commitments (1991). In 2005, Kelly and his brother Seán formed the band Poets of the Fall, who have released five albums. The RS-3 is a member of the GE Genesis family of locomotives. The RS-3 is also used by several other railroads, including the Norfolk Southern Railway, the Burlington Northern Santa Fe, the Canadian Pacific Railway, and the NS Elite. An tAthair an tIúisce Maraí (11th Mississippi Infantry) monument is an American Civil War monument in Adams County, Pennsylvania, United States. It is located in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania. It is a contributing property in the National Register of Historic Places listings for Gettysburg National Military Park. The monument was erected in 1863 and dedicated on November 11, 1863, by the 11th Mississippi Infantry. The monument is a granite obelisk, with a bronze plaque on its base. The monument is situated at the intersection of South Cedar Street and Gettysburg Avenue in the town of Adams, about one mile (1.6 km) northeast of the Gettysburg National Military Park battlefield. It is a contributing property in the National Register of Historic Places listings for Gettysburg National Military Park. It is a contributing property in the National Register of Historic Places listings for Gettysburg National Military Park. It is a contributing property in the National Register of Historic Places listings for Gettysburg National Military Park. The monument was erected in 1863 and dedicated on November 11, 1863, by the 11th Mississippi Infantry. The monument is a granite obelisk, with a bronze plaque on its base. The monument is situated at the intersection of South Cedar Street and Gettysburg Avenue in the town of Adams, about one mile (1.6 km) northeast of the Gettysburg National Military Park battlefield. It is a contributing property in the National Register of Historic Places listings for Gettysburg National Military Park. An tAthair an tIúisce Maraí (11th Mississippi Infantry) monument is an American Civil War monument in Adams County, Pennsylvania, United States. It is located in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania

The Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca is a football stadium in Arapiraca, Alagoas. It is the home ground of ASA. It is also known as Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca, Estádio Coaracy Fonseca, and Estádio da ASA. It has a capacity of 17,000 people. The stadium was built in 2007. It is named after former ASA president Coaracy da Mata Fonseca.  ASA is a football club in Arapiraca, Alagoas, Brazil. It plays in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C. It was founded in 1927. It is nicknamed Asa Gigante (Giant Wing; the name of a former Brazilian airline). It is the largest football club in Alagoas. The club was founded by teachers and students from the state-run Arapiraca College.  The Campeonato Brasileiro Série C is a football competition in Brazil. It is the third tier of the Brazilian football league system. It was established in 1971. It is the third division of the Brazilian Championship. The competition is contested by 48 teams. The winner of the competition qualifies for the next year's Campeonato Brasileiro Série B. The competition is held annually. The clubs are divided into 12 groups of four teams. Each group plays a round-robin tournament, with each team playing each other once. The two best teams in each group qualify for the quarter-finals. From there, the teams play a knockout tournament until the final. The champion of the competition qualifies for the next year's Campeonato Brasileiro Série B.  The clubs are divided into five regions: Northeast, North, Southeast, South and Midwest. The competition is divided into five stages: group stage, quarter-finals, semi-finals, third-place playoff and final. The group stage is held in two rounds. The first round is played in a double round-robin format. The second round is played in a single round-robin format. The top four teams in each group qualify for the quarter-finals. The quarter-finals are played as a single-elimination tournament. The semi-finals are played as a single-elimination tournament. The third-place playoff is played as a single-elimination tournament. The final is played as a single-elimination tournament. The club with the best performance in the previous year's Campeonato Brasileiro Série B is given a bye to the quarter-finals. Born in Leningrad, U.S.S.R. on November 8, 1932. Died in St. Petersburg, Russia on December 9, 1991. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva was a Russian mathematician and economist. Bondareva was a leading expert in the theory of games, game theory, and game programming. She was a professor of economics at St. Petersburg State University. Bondareva graduated from St. Petersburg State University in 1953. In 1959 she defended her dissertation, "On the mathematical theory of games". In the late 1950s and early 1960s, Bondareva developed a mathematical theory of the games of chess and checkers. Her work was based on the theory of Markov chains and the theory of differential equations. She was the first to introduce the notion of a game with incomplete information. She was awarded the Lenin Komsomol Prize in 1970. In the late 1960s, Bondareva was one of the first economists to apply mathematical methods to economics. She was one of the first to study the theory of oligopolies. She was the first to apply the theory of differential equations to the problem of the optimal behavior of firms. Bondareva also worked in the theory of markets, in the theory of financial markets and in the theory of auctions. In her work, she used the methods of mathematical statistics and stochastic processes. Bondareva was a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences and a corresponding member of the Academy of Sciences of Ukraine. She was the first woman to be elected a member of the International Economic Association. She was a member of the board of directors of the Mathematical Institute of the Ural Branch of the Russian Academy of Sciences. She was the author of more than 120 scientific works. She died in St. Petersburg, Russia on December 9, 1991.

An ALCO RS-3 was a class of American light rail cars. It was the first series of light rail cars built by the Alco Car and Foundry Company. The RS-3 was introduced in May 1950. The RS-3 was a high-floor, articulated, electric multiple unit. The cars were built in several versions, including a variant with an articulated diesel engine. Chinabank, an Ayala corporation, is a publicly traded company incorporated in the Philippines. Its principal subsidiaries include the Chinabank Foundation, a philanthropic organization, and Chinabank Foundation Holdings, Inc., a for-profit company. The company was founded in the Philippines in 1981 by the Insular Government of the Philippines, which is known today as the Philippine Government. Chinabank is headquartered in Manila, Philippines. The company is part of the Ayala Group, one of the Philippines’ largest conglomerates. Ayala Corporation is the largest private corporation in the Philippines and has a presence in the fields of banking, telecommunications, energy, construction, real estate, manufacturing, retailing, and food processing.

Darlington is a town in County Durham, England. It is situated on the River Wear. The town is at the intersection of the A1(M) and A1 roads. It is part of the Darlington urban area, which has a population of 94,000. The town is home to the headquarters of the National Grid, which supplies electricity to the UK and Ireland. The town has a railway station, which is part of the North East England line. It was home to the Darlington Race Course, which was used to race horses from 1867 until it closed in 1973. The course was a Grade 1 racecourse. The town is the birthplace of the actress Dame Angela Lansbury. An ALCO RS-3 was a class of locomotive used by the Great Western Railway (GWR) and its successors, the British Railways (BR) and the current Network Rail. It was built by American Locomotive Company (ALCO) in the United States of America, and delivered to the GWR in May 1950 - August 1956.  The RS-3 was designed to operate on the GWR's West Country main line between London Paddington and Exeter, and on its branch lines to Bath, Bristol, Plymouth and Yeovil. The RS-3s were the first GWR locomotives to have their main frames constructed from welded steel, and they were the first to have their tenders built with internal cabs. The RS-3s were the first GWR locomotives to have air-operated brake cylinders, and were the last to be fitted with main steam pipes and valves.  The RS-3 was powered by a four-stroke engine, which developed 800 bhp at 2300 rpm. The RS-3 was constructed to a length of 17068.8 (millimetres), and was fitted with a tender with a water capacity of 3,200 imperial gallons (17,400 litres).  ALCO RS-3 locomotives were renumbered by the BR in 1951, and were finally withdrawn from service in June 1967.

The Velvet Underground & Nico is a proto-punk rock album by the American rock band The Velvet Underground, released in March 1967 on the independent label Vanguard Records. It is widely considered one of the most important records of the 1960s and has been cited as one of the most important albums of all time. The album's sound, which incorporated elements of doo-wop, classical music, and avant-garde rock, helped pave the way for punk rock, glam rock, and new wave. In 2003, Rolling Stone magazine ranked it the sixth-best album of all time, and it is listed at number 99 on the magazine's list of the "500 Greatest Albums of All Time".

The Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca is a football stadium in Arapiraca, Alagoas. It is the home ground of Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense. It was inaugurated on November 29, 2005, and has a maximum capacity of 17,000 people. It is currently used mostly for association football, and also for other sports such as futsal and American football. The Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is a football club from Arapiraca, Alagoas, Brazil. It plays in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C. It was founded in 1941. It is one of the most successful clubs from Alagoas, with six state titles, four regional titles, and one national title. The Vila Nova Futebol Clube is a football club from Goiânia, Goiás, Brazil. It was founded on April 8, 1952. It currently plays in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C. It is the most successful club from Goiás, with eight state titles, one regional title, and one national title. The Campeonato Brasileiro Série C is a football competition in Brazil. It is the third level of the Brazilian football league system. It is organized by the Brazilian Football Confederation (CBF). It is contested by 20 clubs, who are divided into two groups of 10. The top four clubs of each group advance to the second stage, where they are divided into two groups of four. The two first clubs of each group advance to the third stage, where they are divided into two groups of two. The two first clubs of each group advance to the fourth stage, where they play against each other in a two-legged playoff. The winner of the final plays against the winner of the Campeonato Brasileiro Série D for a place in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série B in the following year. Alan Shepard, an American astronaut, was born on 18 November 1923 in New Hampshire. He died on 28 August 1998 in California. Alan Shepard was a U.S. astronaut who was the first American in space, on a sub-orbital flight in 1961. He was also the first American to die in space, in a 1967 spacewalk. Shepard was born in New Hampshire and was educated in the state. He later moved to California and entered the U.S. Navy. In 1954, he was selected to be a member of the astronaut program. Shepard was a member of the Apollo 14 mission in 1971, but the mission was canceled due to the failure of Apollo 13. He later worked as a NASA administrator, serving as Chief of the Astronaut Office from 1963 to 1967. Shepard was awarded the Distinguished Service Medal (United States Navy) in 1961. In 1998, he was awarded the Congressional Space Medal of Honor. In 1999, he was awarded the Presidential Medal of Freedom.

An Phoblacht, the official newspaper of the Irish Republican Army, was founded in 1905 by John O'Mahony. It was first published as a weekly paper, but was later changed to a daily. The paper was published by Cumann na mBan. The first issue was published on St. Patrick's Day, March 17, 1905. The paper was published in Irish and English, and was the first Irish newspaper to be published in both languages. The first English language issue was published in 1907. The newspaper was a combination of politics and humor. The newspaper was published until the Easter Rising in 1916. The newspaper was published by the Irish Republican Army during the Easter Rising. The paper was printed in French, German and English. An Phoblacht was a newspaper of the Irish Republican Army. The paper was a weekly paper published in Dublin. Stahl and the screenplay was written by Gladys Unger. The film stars Greer Garson, Walter Pidgeon, Ruth Hussey, Mary Boland, Laurence Olivier and Charles Laughton. Turn Me On, album by The Pogues, is a genre-bending punk rock album that began as a collaboration between The Pogues and The Dubliners. The album was released in May 1985. The album was a critical and commercial success, selling over five million copies worldwide. The album also gave the band its first and only number one single, the title track, which was also the band's only top 40 hit. The album was nominated for Best Album at the 1985 Brit Awards, but lost to David Bowie's Let It Bleed. The album was certified double platinum in the United States in March 1986 and is now certified six times platinum.

Miller Hall is a four story building, constructed in 1958, located on the corner of South Main Street and East Broad Street, in Williamsburg, Virginia. It is named for the first president of the College of William and Mary, which is now part of the University of Virginia, and is located near the College of William and Mary campus. The building is located at the intersection of South Main Street and East Broad Street, on the site of the former Williamsburg Inn, a hotel that was destroyed in a fire in the late 1940s. The Velvet Underground was an American rock band formed in 1964 in New York City. It was one of the most influential and important groups of the 1960s counterculture and alternative music scene. The band was formed in 1964 by Lou Reed and John Cale, who were later joined by Sterling Morrison and Maureen Tucker. The band's original lineup lasted until 1970, when Tucker left to become a mother, and Reed and Morrison disbanded the group to pursue their own projects. Reed formed a new band, Transformer, with Tucker and Doug Yule, while Cale and Morrison formed The Modern Lovers. The Velvet Underground's self-titled debut album was released in 1967 to critical acclaim. It was an important influence on the development of punk rock and new wave music in the late 1970s. The Velvet Underground's songs were mostly written by Reed, and their distinctive sound was characterized by Reed's experimental songwriting and Cale's experimental and classical-inspired music. Their second album, White Light/White Heat, was released in 1968. Their final album, the 1970 live Loaded, was released after the group's disbandment, and it was a commercial success. The Velvet Underground's career was cut short by Reed's drug problems and a lack of commercial success. The band's early recordings were reissued in the 1990s as part of the bootleg series, which has become a popular genre of music collecting. Their debut album was ranked number 26 on Rolling Stone's list of the 500 greatest albums of all time, and their song "All Tomorrow's Parties" was ranked number 36 on the magazine's list of the 500 greatest songs of all time. In 2003, the group was inducted into the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame. In 2009, Rolling Stone placed them at number 25 on its list of the "100 Greatest Artists of All Time". The Velvet Underground was formed by John Cale, Lou Reed, Sterling Morrison and Maureen Tucker. Their debut album, The Velvet Underground & Nico, was released in 1967, and it was an underground hit. Their second album, White Light/White Heat, was released in 1968, and it featured the song "All Tomorrow's Parties", which was written by Reed. The Velvet Underground disbanded in 1970. Alan Shepard, an American astronaut, was born on 18 November 1923, in New Hampshire. He was selected by NASA in 1959 and served as Chief of the Astronaut Office from 1963 to 1969. Shepard died on 20 July 1998, in California. He is best remembered for the first American spacewalk, which he performed on 5 May 1962, during the flight of the Mercury capsule Freedom 7.

Alan Shepard, an American astronaut, was born on 18 November 1923 in New Hampshire. He died on 28 February 1998 in California. Alan Shepard was a U.S. Navy test pilot who was the first American in space. He was also the first American to walk in space. Alan Shepard served as Chief of the Astronaut Office in the 1960s. He was the commander of the Apollo 14 mission in 1971. Alan Shepard was awarded the Distinguished Service Medal (United States Navy) in 1971.

Liselotte Grschebina is a German-Jewish pianist, composer, and conductor. She was born in Stuttgart, Germany and began her musical studies at age four. She studied at the Stuttgart Hochschule für Musik und Theater, and at the Mozarteum Salzburg. She is also a graduate of the Jerusalem Academy of Music and Dance. Grschebina was awarded the Israel Prize in 2013. Israel is a country in Western Asia. It is bordered by the Mediterranean Sea, Lebanon, Syria, the Jordan River, the Gulf of Aqaba, and the Egyptian Sinai Peninsula. The area of Israel is 20,770 km2 (7,700 sq mi) and the population is 8,429,000. Modern Standard Arabic is the official language. The capital and largest city is Jerusalem. An ALCO RS-3 was a class of locomotive built by the American Locomotive Company (ALCO) from 1950 to 1956. The RS-3 was a diesel-electric locomotive, with a single 12-cylinder diesel engine driving an electric generator which powered the traction motors. The RS-3 was also the first ALCO locomotive to use an all-steel frame. The RS-3 was used in many parts of the United States and Canada, and was the last ALCO locomotive built for the American railroads. The ALCO RS-3 was also used by the Canadian Pacific Railway, Canadian National Railway, and the Santa Fe Railway. The ALCO RS-3 was built in a total of five different classes. The first class was the ALCO RS-3A, which was built between 1950 and 1953, and had a total of 744 locomotives built. The second class was the ALCO RS-3B, which was built between 1950 and 1952, and had a total of 147 locomotives built. The third class was the ALCO RS-3C, which was built between 1950 and 1954, and had a total of 1,099 locomotives built. The fourth class was the ALCO RS-3D, which was built between 1951 and 1953, and had a total of 923 locomotives built. The fifth class was the ALCO RS-3E, which was built between 1951 and 1953, and had a total of 1,008 locomotives built. The ALCO RS-3 was the first ALCO locomotive to be built with an all-steel frame. The ALCO RS-3 was also the first ALCO locomotive to have a diesel engine in the locomotive's nose, instead of at the back of the locomotive. The ALCO RS-3 was also the first ALCO locomotive to have a cab at the front of the locomotive, instead of at the back. The ALCO RS-3 was also the first ALCO locomotive to have a roof-mounted pantograph. The ALCO RS-3 was also the first ALCO locomotive to have a single-cylinder diesel engine, instead of a multi-cylinder diesel engine. Sludge metal is an American rock subgenre, with heavy metal and sludge metal elements. The earliest known bands were the Melvins and Neurosis in the early 1980s. Sludge metal has also been called Stoner metal, Doom metal, and Sludge-doom metal. In the early 1990s, bands like Eyehategod, Crowbar, Down, and Corrosion of Conformity began to emerge. These bands were influenced by the Melvins, Neurosis, and other early doom metal bands. Many of these bands came from the same area of the United States, with the scene centered in the Mississippi and Louisiana area. Many of these bands are also considered to be from the Southern metal genre. The term "sludge metal" was first used by Scott Reeder of the Melvins to describe the music of Eyehategod and other bands in the early 1990s. The term gained popularity in the mid 1990s. Other bands of the early 1990s include High on Fire, Down, Crowbar, Eyehategod, Corrosion of Conformity, Sleep, and Baroness. In the early 2000s, sludge metal gained a wider audience, with bands like Isis, Mastodon, Baroness, and High on Fire becoming more popular. Later, bands like Baroness, Kylesa, and Sleep began to gain a wider audience, and the genre began to be considered as a commercial success. In the 2010s, sludge metal bands such as Baroness, Kylesa, High on Fire, and Sleep have continued to gain popularity, and the genre has been considered to be one of the most popular subgenres of metal. Other popular bands include Eyehategod, Crowbar, Down, Corrosion of Conformity, and High on Fire.

An ALCO RS-3 was a class of locomotive built by the American Locomotive Company (ALCO) from 1950 to 1956. The RS-3 was a 12-cylinder, air-cooled, electric locomotive. The RS-3 was built as a replacement for the ALCO RS-2 and RS-1. The RS-3 was also built for export, for example in Ireland, where it was named the ALCO RS-3. The ALCO RS-3 was a successful model, and was built for both passenger and freight service. The ALCO RS-3 was also built for export, for example in Ireland, where it was named the ALCO RS-3. An ALCORS-3 built for the London and North Eastern Railway in 1952 is preserved at the Severn Valley Railway.  The ALCO RS-3 was a 4-6-0 steam locomotive built by American Locomotive Company in the United States for the London and North Eastern Railway in the late 1940s and early 1950s. It was one of the last steam locomotives to be built for the LNER.  The locomotive was of the B9 design, and was a development of the ALCO RS-2. The first RS-3s were built to the B9.1 specification, and were the most powerful steam locomotives built for the LNER. The last RS-3s built were the B9.3, which had a more powerful boiler and larger superheater surface.  The RS-3 was one of the most successful LNER locomotives, and was used extensively on the main lines and on the branch lines of the LNER network. Many were modified to RS-3A specification, which included an additional superheater surface, and were used on the branch lines. These locomotives were often given the name of the branch line they served, such as the "East Coast Express", which served the East Coast Main Line.  The RS-3 was also exported to the Southern Railway, where it was used on the main lines and branch lines. One example was the "Stockport Express", which ran between London and Manchester.  The RS-3 was superseded by the BR Standard Class 03 diesel-hydraulic locomotives, and the last steam locomotive to be built for the LNER was withdrawn in 1960.  The RS-3 is preserved at the Severn Valley Railway, and the East Coast Express is preserved at the National Railway Museum.

An ALCO RS-3 was a class of 1,700-ton, 17068.8-millimetre (6 ft 8 3⁄8 in × 5 ft 3 1⁄2 in) long, side-loading coal hopper car built by the American Locomotive Company in the late 1940s and early 1950s. The car had a short-lived career, being replaced in service by the ALCO RS-4, a larger version of the same design. The RS-3 was designed to haul large quantities of coal from mines in the West to fuel the emerging steel mills of the East. Although the design was intended to be simple, it proved to be difficult to build and maintain. The RS-3 was the first car built by ALCO to use the vertical, two-piece coal hopper that would later be used on many other ALCO designs. The RS-3 was also the first car to be produced with a welded construction, and the first to use the modern steam generator boiler. The RS-3 was used in the Illinois Central Railroad, which was later merged into the Illinois Central System. In the 1950s, the ICS was the largest coal-hauling railroad in the United States, and it was the only railroad in the country to use the RS-3.  The ICS RS-3 was used until the early 1960s, when it was replaced by the larger, more modern ALCO RS-4, which was essentially an RS-3 with a longer body and an additional pair of coal hoppers. The RS-3s were the last of the steam locomotives used by the ICS, which was fully converted to diesel power in the 1960s. The RS-3 was a heavy, lumbering locomotive, and was nicknamed the "Iron Horse". Alan Shepard, an American astronaut, was born on 18 November 1923, in New Hampshire. He died in California in 1998. Alan Shepard was a United States Air Force pilot and test pilot. In 1963, he was appointed as the Chief of the Astronaut Office. He was the first American to fly in space, on May 5, 1961, aboard Freedom 7. In 1962, he became the first American to command a space flight, on a mission aboard Freedom 7. He was the first American to fly in space twice, on June 15, 1965, aboard Freedom 7. He was also the first American to command a space flight twice, on a mission aboard Apollo 14, on February 7, 1971. He was the youngest man to fly in space, at the age of 33, in 1961. He was the oldest man to fly in space, at the age of 57, in 1971. He was the first man to have an ejection seat in a spacecraft. Alan Shepard was born in New Hampshire. He graduated from the Naval War College, in 1957, with a master's degree in naval science. He was a Navy pilot and test pilot. Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna (born 1924), known for the Bondareva–Shapley theorem, is a Soviet mathematician known for her work in combinatorial geometry and theoretical computer science. She was a professor of mathematics at the Moscow State University, and is the author of more than 150 papers in mathematics and physics. She was elected to the Russian Academy of Sciences in 1982.

Its best performance in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C was when it won the competition in 2013, with Vila Nova Futebol Clube as their champions. It is the largest football club in the city, with 17,000 members.  The club's full name is Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense. It is commonly known as ASA. An ALCO RS-3 was a class of 4-6-2 locomotive built by the American Locomotive Company for the Southern Pacific Railroad (SP). The class was designed to meet a requirement from SP to replace the aging Baldwin 4-6-2 Pacifics that had been in service since the early 1900s. The new class was to be capable of hauling the SP's heaviest freight trains, and to be more powerful than the Baldwin units. ALCO built a total of 1418 RS-3s, which were built in two main groups. The first group, consisting of 1013 locomotives, was built between 1950 and 1956. These locomotives were the last ALCOs built with side frames and a center buffer. The second group, consisting of 905 locomotives, was built between 1964 and 1970. These units had a modified design with the center buffer removed and replaced with a centerplate and a buffer beam, and the cab moved forward to accommodate the larger centerplate. The second group had a number of other minor differences from the first group, such as a different type of air cleaner, a different type of smokebox, and different valve gear. Both groups were built with the same wheel arrangement, consisting of 24 x 2.25 ft (0.7 m) driving wheels and 48 x 1.25 ft (0.4 m) trailing wheels. The RS-3s were also the last ALCO locomotives to use a mechanical regulator for controlling the steam pressure in the boiler. They were succeeded by the ALCO RS-4, which was built with a more modern cab design.  The RS-3 was the first ALCO locomotive to use a cab with a modern "glass dome". It also had a new type of cab heater, which was more effective at removing moisture from the cab, and a cab air conditioner. The RS-3 was the first ALCO locomotive to use a mechanical regulator to control the boiler pressure. The RS-3 was also the first ALCO locomotive to use a cab-mounted air horn. The RS-3 was built with a number of different types of tenders, including tenders with a coal capacity of 50 long tons (51 t; 54 short tons), 100 long tons (101 t; 110 short tons), or 150 long tons (160 t; 170 short tons). An ALCO RS-3 was a class of locomotive used by the Great Western Railway (GWR) and its successors, the British Railways (BR) and the current Network Rail. It was also used by the London and North Eastern Railway (LNER) and the London Midland and Scottish Railway (LMS). The locomotive was built by ALCO, in May 1950 - August 1956. It was a diesel-electric locomotive with a 17068.8 (millimetres) length.

Alan B. Miller Hall is currently the home of the Mason School of Business, and was the first building on the campus of the College of William and Mary in Williamsburg, Virginia. It is named for the first president of the college, John Parke Custis, and is the only building on the campus to bear his name.  It was designed by the firm of McKim, Mead and White and was dedicated in 1914. It is a two-story limestone building with a large, domed rotunda in the center. The building is situated on the banks of the James River and has a large porch facing the river. The porch is supported by four Ionic columns.  In the 1930s, the building was used by the college as a dormitory. The building was converted to a museum in the 1970s, and the college began to use the building for events and meetings. The museum was closed in the 1980s and the building was restored. The building is now used for meetings, special events, and as a gallery space for temporary exhibitions.  Alan B. Miller Hall is listed on the National Register of Historic Places. It is also a contributing building to the Colonial Williamsburg Historic District. The building is owned by the College of William and Mary.  Alan B. Miller Hall is located on the campus of the College of William and Mary, in Williamsburg, Virginia. It is located on the banks of the James River and is the only building on the campus to bear the name of the first president of the college, John Parke Custis. The building was designed by the firm of McKim, Mead and White and was dedicated in 1914. It is a two-story limestone building with a large, domed rotunda in the center. The building is situated on the banks of the James River and has a large porch facing the river. The porch is supported by four Ionic columns.  In the 1930s, the building was used by the college as a dormitory. The building was converted to a museum in the 1970s, and the college began to use the building for events and meetings. The museum was closed in the 1980s and the building was restored. The building is now used for meetings, special events, and as a gallery space for temporary exhibitions.  Alan B. Bondareva, Olga Nikolaevna (1927–2011), mathematician, was born in Saint Petersburg. She received a diploma in mathematics from the Leningrad State University in 1953 and a Ph.D. in 1955. From 1956 to 1958 she worked in the Mathematical Institute of the Academy of Sciences of the USSR, and from 1958 to 1964 she worked in the Steklov Mathematical Institute of the Academy of Sciences of the USSR. In 1964 she was appointed professor of mathematics at the Leningrad State University, where she taught until her retirement in 1992. Bondareva was a specialist in the theory of functions of a complex variable. She is known for her contributions to the theory of analytic functions in the unit disk, to the theory of orthogonal polynomials, and to the theory of entire functions. In 1971 she was elected corresponding member of the USSR Academy of Sciences and in 1984 full member. Bondareva died in Saint Petersburg.
Olga Bondareva is an Leningrad State University graduate.  Olga Bondareva is an Leningrad State University graduate.

Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport is operated by ENAIRE, the Spanish air navigation service provider. It is located in Alcobendas, Madrid, Spain. The airport has four runways. It is located 610 metres above sea level.  Madrid is the capital and the largest city of Spain. It is the third most populous city in the European Union, with 3,223,537 inhabitants within its city limits in 2017. Madrid is the seat of the Community of Madrid and of the Autonomous Community of Madrid, and the third-largest metropolitan area in the European Union with an estimated population of 6,255,991.  ENAIRE is the Spanish air navigation service provider. It is responsible for the management of Spanish airspace, air navigation services, air traffic control and the provision of meteorological information to the aviation sector.  Alcobendas is a town and municipality in the Community of Madrid, Spain. It is located in the metropolitan area of Madrid. The town of Alcobendas is located 5.7 kilometres (3.6 mi) to the north-west of Madrid. The municipality is located in the north of the autonomous community and is bordered by the municipalities of San Sebastián de los Reyes, Madrid, Paracuellos de Jarama and Coslada. The municipality has a total area of 8.64 km² (3.37 sq mi), of which 8.52 km² (3.33 sq mi) is land and 0.12 km² (0.046 sq mi) is water.  Alcobendas is a town of 75,000 inhabitants located in the north of Madrid. It has a great industrial and commercial activity. Its economy is based on the services sector, with a strong presence of large companies. It is a town with a great cultural and sports offer, with a large number of cultural associations and sports clubs.  The airport has four runways, two of which are 4,000 metres long. It has a single terminal, T1, which is divided into three sections, each with its own security checkpoint. The airport has a total of 90 check-in desks, and the terminal has three boarding gates, each with two jetways. The airport has four jetbridges. The arrest of the former justice minister, who was in charge of the country’s anti-corruption commission, is one of the biggest political scandals in Mexico in years. Mr Gil Zuarth, a close ally of President Enrique Pena Nieto, was arrested along with his wife, Laura Vargas, and a former member of the National Assembly, Jorge Luis Lavalle. Mr Gil Zuarth, who is a member of the ruling Institutional Revolutionary Party (PRI), resigned as justice minister in September 2014. He was replaced by attorney general Jesus Murillo Karam. The three suspects are accused of receiving millions of dollars from the Brazilian construction company Odebrecht, which is facing corruption allegations in Latin America. The arrests are the first of several expected as Mexican authorities investigate the Odebrecht case. Mexico’s anti-corruption commission, headed by Mr Gil Zuarth, has been suspended as a result of the arrests. An tOllalais Gaeilge Coillte (T.G.C.) is an independent cultural body whose principal purpose is to promote the use of the Irish language. It is a voluntary organisation with no political or religious affiliations. T.G.C. is the national body for Irish language and culture in the Republic of Ireland and the only national body for the Irish language in the world. T.G.C. is also a registered charity. T.G.C. was founded in 1909 in Dublin by a group of enthusiasts including Dr. William Butler Yeats, Padraic Colum, John MacBride and others. In 1979 T.G.C. was granted charitable status under the Charities Act. T.G.C. is made up of a National Council, which is the governing body, and a Secretariat, which is the operational arm of the organisation. The Secretariat is based in Dublin. The Council is made up of representatives from the Irish language communities throughout Ireland, and the island of Great Britain. It meets every three years to set policy and elect a new Board of Management. The T.G.C. has a full-time staff of about sixty people and a permanent establishment of over one million euro. The organisation is funded through the Department of Arts, Sport and Tourism, the Department of Education and Science, the Department of Health and Children, the Department of Justice, Equality and Law Reform, the Department of the Environment, Heritage and Local Government, and the Office of Public Works. The Irish Government also supports the publication of Irish language books and periodicals. The T.G.C. is also funded through the European Union through the European Regional Development Fund. The T.G.C. also receives funding from other sources such as the Arts Council of Ireland, the Department of Foreign Affairs and the Heritage Council. T.G.C. operates through its own national offices and through local branches throughout Ireland and the island of Great Britain. It also operates through a network of schools, libraries, museums, arts centres, language centres, music schools, drama groups, literary organisations and other cultural bodies throughout Ireland and the island of Great Britain. The T.G.C. also works with the Irish communities overseas and with the Irish communities in the Republic of Ireland. T.G.C.'s principal aim is to promote and develop the Irish language and culture in Ireland and the island of Great Britain

Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport is the main airport of Spain, located in the city of Madrid, and is the principal hub for Spanish flag carrier Iberia. It is located approximately 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) north of downtown Madrid, and is the second-busiest airport in Spain, after Barcelona-El Prat Airport, serving a total of over 40 million passengers in 2018. It is owned by the Spanish state-owned company Aena. The airport is named after the Spanish politician Adolfo Suárez González, who served as the first president of the Spanish government after the death of Francisco Franco in 1975, and died in 2014. The airport is the main hub of Iberia, with the headquarters of the company located in the airport. Iberia's main base is located at Terminal 4. The Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca is a football stadium in Arapiraca, Alagoas. It is the home ground of Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense. It was inaugurated on November 29, 2005, and has a maximum capacity of 17,000 people. It is currently used mostly for football matches, and also for other sports such as volleyball and handball. Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is a football club in Arapiraca, Alagoas. It plays in Campeonato Brasileiro Série C, the third tier of the Brazilian football league system. It was founded on November 1, 2005, and plays its home matches at Estádio Coaracy da Mata Fonseca. Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is the most successful club in Alagoas, having won the state championship 15 times, and the Campeonato Alagoano twice, in 2008 and 2010. In 2015 the club was promoted to the second tier, the Campeonato Brasileiro Série B, after winning the Campeonato Alagoano for the third time in four years. They were relegated to Série C after finishing 16th in the 2016 Série B, with three wins, eight draws and 12 losses. They were the last team promoted to the Série C, and the last team relegated to the Série D. The club has 17,000 members. Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is nicknamed Fantasma das Alagoas (Alagoas Phantom). It was founded on November 1, 2005. An Phoblacht editor Geof Bartz died on a factory farm.  An Phoblacht editor Geof Bartz died on a factory farm.
An Phoblacht, the official newspaper of the Republican Sinn Féin party, carried the first edition of the Republican Proclamation on Easter Monday, 1916. It was signed by Eamon de Valera, Seán Mac Diarmada and Arthur Griffith. The Proclamation was a call for a Republic to be established in Ireland, and it contained the following: “We proclaim to the Irish nation that the Irish Republic is an accomplished fact, and that its sovereignty is based upon the will of the Irish people.” The Proclamation was published on the morning of Easter Monday, 1916. The Provisional Government, established by the Republican leaders, had been in place since the previous November. In the first few weeks of its existence, the Provisional Government was based in Dublin Castle. It was made up of republicans, nationalists and socialists, including some members of the Irish Volunteers. The Provisional Government was ousted by the British in May 1916, and the leadership of the Irish Republic was moved to the Curragh Camp, a training camp for the Irish Volunteers. In June 1916, the Provisional Government moved to the Mansion House in Dublin, where it remained until the end of the War of Independence in 1923. The Irish Republic was proclaimed on Easter Monday, 1916, but the war of independence did not end until August 1921, when the Treaty of 1921 was signed.

An Phoblacht, the official newspaper of the Irish Republican Army, was published weekly from the beginning of 1916 until its closure in 1918. The newspaper was established in Dublin in January 1916, with a weekly print run of around 20,000 copies. It was the most widely circulated Irish language newspaper in Ireland during the Irish War of Independence and the Irish Civil War. It was published by volunteers throughout the war and was one of the few publications to remain in print throughout the conflict. The newspaper was founded by Michael Collins, Eoin MacNeill and Sean MacDermott. An Phoblacht was a left-wing newspaper that supported the republican movement. It was published in both Irish and English.

Brandon Carter, a professor of physics at the University of California, Santa Barbara, was born in England on June 5, 1945. Carter's main research field is general relativity, and he is best known for his contributions to the field of astrophysics, in particular the Carter constant and the no-hair theorem. Carter earned his doctoral degree in physics from Cambridge University in 1973, and in 1974 he became a lecturer at the University of Illinois, Urbana-Champaign. Carter's first academic appointment was as a professor of physics at the University of California, Santa Barbara, where he is currently a professor of physics. Carter's research has been funded by the National Science Foundation, the Department of Energy, and the National Aeronautics and Space Administration. Carter is a member of the American Physical Society and the American Association for the Advancement of Science.

The Quine Tapes is a bootleg series of The Velvet Underground's first two albums. The series was released in 1996 by Forgotten Records. The original recordings were made by band manager Doug Yule on a reel-to-reel tape recorder during the recording of the first two albums. The first release was in 1996, and the second in 1997. Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport is the main airport of Spain, serving the capital city of Madrid. It is located in the municipality of Alcobendas in the autonomous community of Madrid, Spain. It is the second busiest airport in Spain, and the sixth busiest in the European Union. It is the first airport in Europe by the number of passengers, with over 50 million passengers in 2013. The airport is owned by Aena, and is operated by ENAIRE. Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport has two runways, 14L/32R and 14R/32L. The airport is located at an elevation of 610 m (2,000 ft) above the sea level.

Fíor-Ghael French is an Irish director and screenwriter. He is best known for his films English Without Tears (1993), Finding Anna (1997), and Love/Hate (2002).  Fíor-Ghael was born in Dublin and attended the Lyric Theatre School of Acting, where he received his training. He has also studied at the Royal Academy of Dramatic Art in London. He began his career in the theatre and made his debut on the stage in 1986, playing in a production of Macbeth at the Gate Theatre in Dublin. He was the artistic director of the Gate Theatre from 1991 to 1997.  He made his feature film debut in 1992 with the film, English Without Tears. The film was nominated for three Irish Film and Television Awards, and won the Best Irish Feature Film at the 1993 Chicago International Film Festival. In 1997, he directed Finding Anna, a film starring Daniel Day-Lewis and Emily Watson. The film was nominated for the Palme d'Or at the 1998 Cannes Film Festival. In 2002, he directed Love/Hate, which was nominated for the Palme d'Or at the 2002 Cannes Film Festival. In 2004, he directed the film, Finding Julia, starring Emily Watson and Cillian Murphy. The film was nominated for the Palme d'Or at the 2004 Cannes Film Festival.  He has also directed television drama, including the award-winning series, River City, which ran from 1994 to 1998. He was the head of the Irish Film Board from 2001 to 2004. He is currently the artistic director of the Irish Film Institute. He lives in Dublin, Ireland.  He is the son of the Irish novelist, Frank McGuinness.

Petah Tikva, meaning "Opening of Hope", is a city in Israel. It is the third most populous city in Israel, with a population of about 200,000.  Petah Tikva is located on the Sharon Plain, and is surrounded by the Jerusalem Hills to the south, the Judean Hills to the north, the Mediterranean Sea to the west, and the Sharon Plain to the east. The city is located approximately 25 kilometers (16 mi) north of Jerusalem, and about 20 kilometers (12 mi) south of Tel Aviv.  Petah Tikva is one of the most densely populated cities in Israel, and is often described as a large suburb of Tel Aviv.  Petah Tikva was founded in 1909 by a Jewish settlement movement, which purchased land from the Ottoman Empire. The settlement movement was founded by Nahum Sokolow, a Jewish socialist and a pioneer of modern Zionism.  The city is named after the biblical Petah and Tikva, the twin daughters of Zelophehad, the only son of Ephrath. The daughters were born to Zelophehad, who was the first person to receive a portion of the Promised Land in the Bible.  The city is one of the most important in Israel in terms of industry and technology. Many multinational companies have located their R&D facilities in the city, including Intel, Motorola, Nokia, and Microsoft.  The city has a large university campus, which is home to the Technion, the Israel Institute of Technology. The campus is also home to many colleges and institutes of higher learning, including the Petah Tikva Academic College, the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Graduate School of Engineering, the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Graduate School of Management, the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Graduate School of Physics and Astronomy, the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Graduate School of Chemistry, and the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Graduate School of Computer Science.  The city is also home to the Technion Museum of Science and Technology, the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Nature Park, and the Technion-Israel Institute of Technology Arboretum.  The city is also home to many industrial parks, such as the Petah Tikva Industrial Park, the Petah Tikva Technology Park, the Petah Tikva Media Park, the Petah Tikva Aerospace Park, the Petah Tikva BioPark

Benedict Mór de Breadalbane, 1st Marquess of Breadalbane (18 April 1785 – 18 January 1851), styled The Honourable Max until 1823, was a Scottish nobleman and peer. He was the son of John Douglas, 1st Marquess of Breadalbane and Lady Henrietta Wemyss, the only surviving child of the 3rd Duke of Wemyss. He was also a member of the House of Lords. Max was the last surviving child of his parents, and the last surviving male member of the Breadalbane family. His family had been established in Scotland since the early 14th century and his ancestors had been the hereditary Lords of the Isles. He was educated at Eton College, where he was a member of the Eton College Boat Club, and at the Royal Military Academy, Woolwich. He served as a lieutenant in the Royal Engineers and was promoted to captain in 1815. In 1829 he was promoted to major and appointed to command the Royal Engineer detachment in Gibraltar. He was a Colonel in the Royal Engineers from 1839 to 1850, when he was promoted to the rank of lieutenant-colonel. He was also a Deputy Lieutenant of Lanarkshire. In 1837 he was raised to the Peerage of Great Britain as Baron Breadalbane, of Breadalbane in the County of Perth, and also became Marquess of Breadalbane and Earl of Strathallan, with remainder to his heirs male whatsoever. He succeeded his father as Marquess of Breadalbane in 1843 and as Earl of Strathallan in 1847. His mother, Henrietta Wemyss, was the daughter of the 3rd Duke of Wemyss and had inherited the title of Marchioness of Breadalbane in 1814. Max and his wife, the Honourable Mary Adelaide, daughter of William, 4th Earl Bathurst, had no children. They were both buried at the family seat, Strathallan Castle, Perthshire.

Liselotte Grschebina was born on May 2, 1908, in the German Empire in Karlsruhe, the daughter of a German diplomat. She studied in Munich and Berlin, and worked for the German foreign office. In 1938 she married a Polish officer, and the couple fled to France in 1940. In 1942, she was interned by the Germans in a camp in Drancy, and later in Auschwitz, where she died in 1944.

Darinka Dentcheva is an associate professor at the Humboldt University of Berlin. Her research interests include logic programming, deductive databases, and knowledge representation. She obtained her PhD in computer science from the University of Tübingen, Germany, in 1994. In 1995, she was a visiting scientist at the University of California, Berkeley, and in 1998, she was a visiting professor at the University of Erlangen, Germany. From 1997 to 2001, she was a professor of computer science at the University of Potsdam, Germany. In 2001, she moved to the Humboldt University of Berlin. She is married and has a son.

Liselotte Grschebina was born on May 2, 1908 in Riga, Latvia. She studied at the School of Applied Arts in Stuttgart, Germany. She immigrated to Israel in 1951, and worked as a teacher of painting and drawing at the Bezalel Academy of Art and Design in Jerusalem. In 1953 she married the artist Avner Grschebin, and their son Ilan was born in 1957.

Bíorán Ó hEithir (born Brian Kelly, 23 October 1972) is an Irish composer and pianist. His debut album, Expect a Miracle, was released in 2001 to widespread critical acclaim. The album was nominated for Best Irish Album in the 2002 Meteor Awards and won the Best Irish Album award in the 2002 Virgin Media Music Awards. Kelly has written music for television and film and has composed the scores for several plays, including The History Boys, The Great Gatsby and The Little Prince. In 2007 he composed the music for the Oscar-nominated film The Secret Scripture. He is currently based in Los Angeles, California.  Expect a Miracle is an Irish album by composer and pianist Brian Kelly, released in 2001. It was nominated for Best Irish Album in the 2002 Meteor Awards and won the Best Irish Album award in the 2002 Virgin Media Music Awards. The album is a compilation of Kelly's own compositions. It is also a live album, recorded at the Royal College of Music in Dublin. The album has a duration of 54:56.

An ALCO RS-3 was a class of locomotive used by the British Railways from the late 1940s until the 1980s. The class was developed from the ALCO RS-2 and was the first British diesel electric locomotive to be built by ALCO. They were built in the United States by ALCO and shipped to the UK. There were initially 65 locomotives built, later followed by another 59, making a total of 114 locomotives. The locomotives were designed to haul freight trains at high speeds on main lines, with a top speed of 120 miles per hour (190 km/h). The ALCO RS-3 was one of the most successful locomotives ever built by ALCO.
